<p>The city of <b>Bern</b> (<small>German:</small> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_German" title="Help:IPA for German">[bɛrn]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<a href="/wiki/File:De-Bern.ogg" title="File:De-Bern.ogg"><img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/></a> <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1d/De-Bern.ogg" title="De-Bern.ogg">listen</a>)</small>) or <b>Berne</b> (<small>French: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_French" title="Help:IPA for French">[bɛʁn]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <span lang="it"><i>Berna</i></span> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Italian" title="Help:IPA for Italian">[ˈbɛrna]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Romansh_language" title="Romansh language">Romansh</a>: <span lang="rm"><i>Berna</i></span> <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Roh-Berna.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/38/Roh-Berna.ogg" title="Roh-Berna.ogg">[ˈbɛrnɐ]</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Bernese_German" title="Bernese German">Bernese German</a>: <i>Bärn</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Alemannic_German" title="Help:IPA for Alemannic German">[b̥æːrn]</a></span>) is the de facto capital of <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, referred to by the Swiss as their (e.g. in German) <i>Bundesstadt,</i> or "<a href="/wiki/Federal_city" title="Federal city">federal city</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deFacto_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-deFacto-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[note 1]</a></sup> With a population of 141,762 (November 2016), Bern is the fourth most populous city in Switzerland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StatBern_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-StatBern-5">[4]</a></sup> The Bern agglomeration, which includes 36 municipalities, had a population of 406,900 in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agglomeration_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Agglomeration-6">[5]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> had a population of 660,000 in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup> Bern is also the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Bern" title="Canton of Bern">canton of Bern</a>, the second most populous of Switzerland's cantons.</p>
<p>The official language in Bern is (the Swiss variety of Standard) <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Standard_German" title="Swiss Standard German">German</a>, but the most-spoken language is an <a href="/wiki/Alemannic_German" title="Alemannic German">Alemannic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_German_(linguistics)" title="Swiss German (linguistics)">Swiss German</a> dialect, <a href="/wiki/Bernese_German" title="Bernese German">Bernese German</a>.</p>
<p>In 1983, the <a href="/wiki/Old_City_of_Bern" title="Old City of Bern">historic old town</a> in the centre of Bern became a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>. Bern is ranked among the world’s top ten cities for the best quality of life (2010).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also <a href="/wiki/Names_of_European_cities_in_different_languages:_B" title="Names of European cities in different languages: B">Other names of Bern</a></div>
<p>The etymology of the name <i>Bern</i> is uncertain. According to the local legend, based on <a href="/wiki/Folk_etymology" title="Folk etymology">folk etymology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berthold_V,_Duke_of_Z%C3%A4hringen" title="Berthold V, Duke of Zähringen">Berchtold V, Duke of Zähringen</a>, the founder of the city of Bern, vowed to name the city after the first animal he met on the hunt, and this turned out to be a bear. It has long been considered likely that the city was named after the Italian city of <a href="/wiki/Verona" title="Verona">Verona</a>, which at the time was known as <i>Bern</i> in <a href="/wiki/Middle_High_German" title="Middle High German">Middle High German</a>. As a result of the find of the <a href="/wiki/Bern_zinc_tablet" title="Bern zinc tablet">Bern zinc tablet</a> in the 1980s, it is now more common to assume that the city was named after a pre-existing toponym of Celtic origin, possibly <i>*berna</i> "cleft".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup> The bear was the heraldic animal of the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Bern" title="Coat of arms of Bern">seal and coat of arms of Bern</a> from at least the 1220s. The earliest reference to the keeping of live bears in the <i><a href="/wiki/B%C3%A4rengraben" title="Bärengraben">Bärengraben</a></i> dates to the 1440s.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Bern" title="History of Bern">History of Bern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Bern" title="Timeline of Bern">Timeline of Bern</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Untertorbr%C3%BCcke_Tschachtlanchronik.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1852" data-file-width="2200" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Untertorbr%C3%BCcke_Tschachtlanchronik.jpg/170px-Untertorbr%C3%BCcke_Tschachtlanchronik.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Untertorbr%C3%BCcke_Tschachtlanchronik.jpg/255px-Untertorbr%C3%BCcke_Tschachtlanchronik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Untertorbr%C3%BCcke_Tschachtlanchronik.jpg/340px-Untertorbr%C3%BCcke_Tschachtlanchronik.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Untertorbr%C3%BCcke_Tschachtlanchronik.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The construction of the Untertor-bridge in Bern, Tschachtlanchronik, late 15th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>No <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaeological" title="Archaeological">archaeological</a> evidence that indicates a settlement on the site of today′s city centre prior to the 12th century has been found so far. In antiquity, a <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Oppidum" title="Oppidum">oppidum</a></i> stood on the <i>Engehalbinsel</i> (peninsula) north of Bern, fortified since the 2nd century BC (late <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_T%C3%A8ne_period" title="La Tène period">La Tène period</a>), thought to be one of the twelve oppida of the <a href="/wiki/Helvetii" title="Helvetii">Helvetii</a> mentioned by <a href="/wiki/Commentarii_de_Bello_Gallico" title="Commentarii de Bello Gallico">Caesar</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Germania_Superior" title="Germania Superior">Roman era</a>, there was a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallo-Roman" title="Gallo-Roman">Gallo-Roman</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Vicus" title="Vicus">vicus</a></i> on the same site. The Bern zinc tablet has the name <i>Brenodor</i> ("dwelling of Breno"). In the Early Middle Ages, there was a settlement in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B%C3%BCmpliz" title="Bümpliz">Bümpliz</a>, now a city district of Bern, some 4 km (2 mi) from the medieval city.</p>
<p>The medieval city is a foundation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Z%C3%A4hringer" title="Zähringer">Zähringer</a> ruling family, which rose to power in <a href="/wiki/Upper_Burgundy" title="Upper Burgundy">Upper Burgundy</a> in the 12th century. According to 14th century historiography (<i>Cronica de Berno</i>, 1309), Bern was founded in 1191 by <a href="/wiki/Berthold_V,_Duke_of_Z%C3%A4hringen" title="Berthold V, Duke of Zähringen">Berthold V, Duke of Zähringen</a>.</p>
<p>In 1218, after Berthold died without an heir, Bern was made a <a href="/wiki/Free_imperial_city" title="Free imperial city">free imperial city</a> by the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goldene_Handfeste" title="Goldene Handfeste">Goldene Handfeste</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick II</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Swiss_Confederacy">Old Swiss Confederacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Old Swiss Confederacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MerianBern.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2293" data-file-width="3425" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/MerianBern.jpg/220px-MerianBern.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/MerianBern.jpg/330px-MerianBern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/MerianBern.jpg/440px-MerianBern.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MerianBern.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bern in 1638</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1353 Bern joined the <a href="/wiki/Old_Swiss_Confederacy" title="Old Swiss Confederacy">Swiss Confederacy</a>, becoming one of the eight cantons of the formative period of 1353 to 1481. Bern invaded and conquered <a href="/wiki/Aargau" title="Aargau">Aargau</a> in 1415 and <a href="/wiki/Vaud" title="Vaud">Vaud</a> in 1536, as well as other smaller territories; thereby becoming the largest <a href="/wiki/City-state" title="City-state">city-state</a> north of the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>, by the 18th century comprising most of what is today the <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Bern" title="Canton of Bern">canton of Bern</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canton_of_Vaud" title="Canton of Vaud">canton of Vaud</a>.</p>
<p>The city grew out towards the west of the boundaries of the peninsula formed by the river <a href="/wiki/Aare" title="Aare">Aare</a>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Zytglogge" title="Zytglogge">Zytglogge</a></i> tower marked the western boundary of the city from 1191 until 1256, when the <i>Käfigturm</i> took over this role until 1345. It was, in turn, succeeded by the <i><a href="/wiki/Christoffelturm" title="Christoffelturm">Christoffelturm</a></i> (formerly located close to the site of the modern-day railway station) until 1622. During the time of the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, two new fortifications – the so-called big and small <i><a href="/wiki/Schanze" title="Schanze">Schanze</a></i> (entrenchment) – were built to protect the whole area of the peninsula.</p>
<p>After a major <a href="/wiki/Fire" title="Fire">blaze</a> in 1405, the city's original wooden buildings were gradually replaced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Half-timbered" title="Half-timbered">half-timbered</a> houses and subsequently the <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> buildings which came to be characteristic for the Old Town. Despite the waves of <a href="/wiki/Bubonic_plague" title="Bubonic plague">pestilence</a> that hit Europe in the 14th century, the city continued to grow: mainly due to <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a> from the surrounding countryside.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">Modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Modern history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bern was occupied by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_French_Republic" title="First French Republic">French</a> troops in 1798 during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a>, when it was stripped of parts of its territories. It regained control of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernese_Oberland" title="Bernese Oberland">Bernese Oberland</a> in 1802, and following the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> of 1814, it newly acquired the <a href="/wiki/Bernese_Jura" title="Bernese Jura">Bernese Jura</a>. At this time, it once again became the largest canton of the confederacy as it stood during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Restoration_(Switzerland)" title="Restoration (Switzerland)">Restoration</a> and until the secession of the <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Jura" title="Canton of Jura">canton of Jura</a> in 1979. Bern was made the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_City" title="Federal City">Federal City</a> (seat of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Assembly_of_Switzerland" title="Federal Assembly of Switzerland">Federal Assembly</a>) within the new <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_as_a_federal_state" title="Switzerland as a federal state">Swiss federal state</a> in 1848.</p>
<p>A number of congresses of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist" title="Socialist">socialist</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_International" title="First International">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_International" title="Second International">Second Internationals</a> were held in Bern, particularly during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> when Switzerland was neutral; see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bern_International" title="Bern International">Bern International</a>.</p>
<p>The city's population rose from about 5,000 in the 15th century to about 12,000 by 1800 and to above 60,000 by 1900, passing the 100,000 mark during the 1920s. Population peaked during the 1960s at 165,000, and has since decreased slightly, to below 130,000 by 2000. As of November 2016, the resident population stood at 141,762, of which 100,000 were Swiss citizens and 41,762 (31%) resident foreigners. A further estimated 350,000 people live in the immediate <a href="/wiki/Urban_agglomeration" title="Urban agglomeration">urban agglomeration</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aareschlaufe_Bern-East.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1908" data-file-width="2453" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Aareschlaufe_Bern-East.svg/220px-Aareschlaufe_Bern-East.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Aareschlaufe_Bern-East.svg/330px-Aareschlaufe_Bern-East.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Aareschlaufe_Bern-East.svg/440px-Aareschlaufe_Bern-East.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aareschlaufe_Bern-East.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Aare flows in a wide loop around the <a href="/wiki/Old_City_of_Bern" title="Old City of Bern">Old City of Bern</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bern,_Switzerland.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bern%2C_Switzerland.JPG/220px-Bern%2C_Switzerland.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bern%2C_Switzerland.JPG/330px-Bern%2C_Switzerland.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bern%2C_Switzerland.JPG/440px-Bern%2C_Switzerland.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bern,_Switzerland.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of Bern from the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">ISS</a>. The Old City is in the lower, right hand side.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bern lies on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_plateau" title="Swiss plateau">Swiss plateau</a> in the canton of Bern, slightly west of the centre of Switzerland and 20 km (12 mi) north of the <a href="/wiki/Bernese_Alps" title="Bernese Alps">Bernese</a> <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Alps" title="Swiss Alps">Alps</a>. The countryside around Bern was formed by glaciers during the most recent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ice_Age" title="Ice Age">Ice Age</a>. The two mountains closest to Bern are <a href="/wiki/Gurten_(mountain)" title="Gurten (mountain)">Gurten</a> with a height of 864 m (2,835 ft) and <a href="/wiki/Bantiger" title="Bantiger">Bantiger</a> with a height of 947 m (3,107 ft). The site of the old observatory in Bern is the point of origin of the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_coordinate_system" title="Swiss coordinate system">CH1903 coordinate system</a> at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Bern&amp;params=46_57_08.66_N_7_26_22.50_E_region:CH_type:landmark"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">46°57′08.66″N</span> <span class="longitude">7°26′22.50″E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">46.9524056°N 7.4395833°E</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">46.9524056; 7.4395833</span></span></span></a></span>.</p>
<p>The city was originally built on a hilly <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> surrounded by the river Aare, but outgrew natural boundaries by the 19th century. A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Aar_bridges_in_Bern" title="List of Aar bridges in Bern">number of bridges</a> have been built to allow the city to expand beyond the Aare.</p>
<p>Bern is built on very uneven ground. There is an elevation difference of several metres between the inner city districts on the Aare (<a href="/wiki/Mattequartier" title="Mattequartier">Matte</a>, Marzili) and the higher ones (Kirchenfeld, Länggasse).</p>
<p>Bern has an area, as of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, of 51.62 square kilometers (19.93 sq mi). Of this area, 9.79 square kilometers (3.78 sq mi) or 19.0% is used for agricultural purposes, while 17.33 square kilometers (6.69 sq mi) or 33.6% is forested. Of the rest of the land, 23.25 square kilometers (8.98 sq mi) or 45.0% is settled (buildings or roads), 1.06 square kilometers (0.41 sq mi) or 2.1% is either rivers or lakes and 0.16 square kilometers (0.062 sq mi) or 0.3% is unproductive land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BFS_land_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-BFS_land-12">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Of the developed, 3.6% consists of industrial buildings, 21.7% housing and other buildings, and 12.6% is devoted to transport infrastructure. Power and water infrastructure as well as other special developed areas made up 1.1% of the city, while another 6.0% consists of parks, green belts and sports fields. 32.8% of the total land area is heavily forested. Of the agricultural land, 14.3% is used for growing crops and 4.0% is designated to be used as pastures. The rivers and streams provide all the water in the municipality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BFS_land_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-BFS_land-12">[11]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">Subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The municipality is administratively subdivided into six districts (<i>Stadtteile</i>), each of which consists of several quarters (<i>Quartiere</i>).</p>
<div aria-labelledby="Districts_and_quarters_of_Bern" class="navbox" role="navigation" style="padding:3px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Erlacherhof.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="5526" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Erlacherhof.jpg/220px-Erlacherhof.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Erlacherhof.jpg/330px-Erlacherhof.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Erlacherhof.jpg/440px-Erlacherhof.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Erlacherhof.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Erlacherhof</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rathaus_(Bern).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2528" data-file-width="3284" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Rathaus_%28Bern%29.jpg/220px-Rathaus_%28Bern%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Rathaus_%28Bern%29.jpg/330px-Rathaus_%28Bern%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Rathaus_%28Bern%29.jpg/440px-Rathaus_%28Bern%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Bern" title="List of mayors of Bern">List of mayors of Bern</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gemeinderat_(Bern)" title="Gemeinderat (Bern)">Gemeinderat (Bern)</a></div>
<p>The Municipal Council (<b>Gemeinderat</b>) constitutes the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a> government of the City of Bern and operates as a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Collegiate_authority&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Collegiate authority (page does not exist)">collegiate authority</a>. It is composed of five councillors (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de"><i>Gemeinderat/-rätin</i></span>), each presiding over a directorate (<i>Direktion</i>) comprising several departments and bureaus. The president of the executive department acts as <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a> (<i>Stadtpräsident</i>). In the mandate period 2017–2020 (<i>Legislatur</i>) the Municipal Council is presided by <i>Stadtpräsident</i> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alec_von_Graffenried&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alec von Graffenried (page does not exist)">Alec von Graffenried</a>. Departmental tasks, coordination measures and implementation of laws decreed by the City Council are carried by the Municipal Council. The regular election of the Municipal Council by any inhabitant valid to vote is held every four years. Any resident of Bern allowed to vote can be elected as a member of the Municipal Council. Contrary to most other municipalities, the executive government in Berne is selected by means of a system of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">Proporz</a>. The mayor is elected as such as well by public election while the heads of the other directorates are assigned by the collegiate. The executive body holds its meetings in the <a href="/wiki/Junkerngasse" title="Junkerngasse">Erlacherhof</a>, built by architect <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Albrecht_St%C3%BCrler&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Albrecht Stürler (page does not exist)">Albrecht Stürler</a> after 1747.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-GR-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Bern's Municipal Council is made up of two representatives of the SP (<a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Social Democratic Party of Switzerland">Social Democratic Party</a>), and one each of CVP (<a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_People%27s_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Christian Democratic People's Party of Switzerland">Christian Democratic Party</a>), GFL (<i>Grüne Freie Liste</i> a.k.a. Green Free List, who is the newly elected mayor since 2017), and GB (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gr%C3%BCnes_B%C3%BCndnis_Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Grünes Bündnis Bern (page does not exist)">Green Alliance of Berne</a>), giving the left parties a very strong majority of four out of five seats. The last regular election was held on 27 November 2016/15 January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-GR-14">[13]</a></sup></p>

<p>Dr. Jürg Wichtermann is State Chronicler (<i>Staatsschreiber</i>) since 2008. He has been elected by the collegiate.</p>

<p>The City Council (de: <b>Stadtrat</b>, fr: <b>Conseil de ville</b>) holds <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power">legislative power</a>. It is made up of 80 members, with elections held every four years. The City Council decrees regulations and by-laws that are executed by the Municipal Council and the administration. The delegates are selected by means of a system of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>.</p>
<p>The sessions of the City Council are public. Unlike members of the Municipal Council, members of the City Council are not politicians by profession, and they are paid a fee based on their attendance. Any resident of Bern allowed to vote can be elected as a member of the City Council. The parliament holds its meetings in the <i>Stadthaus</i> (Town Hall).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CP_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-CP-17">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The last regular election of the City Council was held on 27 November 2016 for the mandate period (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de"><i>Legislatur</i></span>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr"><i>la législature</i></span>) from 2017 to 2020. Currently the City Council consist of 24 members of the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Social Democratic Party of Switzerland">Social Democratic Party (SP/PS)</a> including 2 members of the junior party <i>JUSO</i>, 9 <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gr%C3%BCnes_B%C3%BCndnis_Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Grünes Bündnis Bern (page does not exist)">Green Alliance of Berne (GB)</a>, 9 <a href="/wiki/FDP.The_Liberals" title="FDP.The Liberals">The Liberals (FDP/PLR)</a>, 9 <a href="/wiki/Swiss_People%27s_Party" title="Swiss People's Party">Swiss People's Party (SVP/UDC)</a>, 8 <i>Grüne Freie Liste (GFL)</i> (Green Free List), 8 <a href="/wiki/Green_Liberal_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Green Liberal Party of Switzerland">Green Liberal Party (glp/pvl)</a> including one member of its junior party <i>jglp</i>, 3 <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Conservative Democratic Party of Switzerland">Conservative Democratic Party (BDP/PBD)</a>, 2 <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_People%27s_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Christian Democratic People's Party of Switzerland">Christian Democratic People's Party (CVP/PDC)</a>, 2 <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_People%27s_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Evangelical People's Party of Switzerland">Evangelical People's Party (EVP/PEV)</a>, 2 <i>Junge Alternative (JA!)</i> (or Young Alternatives), 2 <a href="/wiki/Alternative_Left" title="Alternative Left">Alternative Linke Bern (AL)</a>, 1 <i>Grüne Partei Bern - Demokratische Alternative (GPB-DA)</i> (or Green Party Bern - Democratic Alternative), and 1 <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Party_of_Labour" title="Swiss Party of Labour">Swiss Party of Labour (PdA)</a>.</p>
<p>The following parties combine their parliamentary power in parliamentary groups (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de"><i>Fraktion(en)</i></span>): AL and GPB-DA and PdA (4), SP and JUSO (24), GB and JA! (11), GFL and EVP (10), glp und jglp (8), BDP and CVP (5), FDP (9), and SVP (9). This gives the left parties an absolute majority of 49 seats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elections">Elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Council">National Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: National Council">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_federal_election,_2015" title="Swiss federal election, 2015">2015 federal election</a> for the <a href="/wiki/National_Council_(Switzerland)" title="National Council (Switzerland)">Swiss National Council</a> the most popular party was the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Social Democratic Party of Switzerland">PS</a> which received 34.3% of the vote. The next five most popular parties were the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Green Party of Switzerland">Green Party</a> (17.4%), the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_People%27s_Party" title="Swiss People's Party">UDC</a> (12.4%), and the <a href="/wiki/FDP.The_Liberals" title="FDP.The Liberals">FDP/PLR</a> (9.9%), <a href="/wiki/Green_Liberal_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Green Liberal Party of Switzerland">glp/pvl</a> (9.4%), and the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Conservative Democratic Party of Switzerland">BDP/PBD</a> (7.0%). In the federal election, a total of 48,556 voters were cast, and the <a href="/wiki/Voter_turnout" title="Voter turnout">voter turnout</a> was 56.0%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_and_sister_cities">Twin and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Twin and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Municipal Council of the city of Bern decided against having twinned cities except for a temporary (during the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008" title="UEFA Euro 2008">UEFA Euro 2008</a>) cooperation with the <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austrian</a> city <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">Salzburg</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Bern has a population (as of April 2016) of 141,107. About 34% of the population are resident foreign nationals. Over the 10 years between 2000 and 2010, the population changed at a rate of 0.6%. Migration accounted for 1.3%, while births and deaths accounted for −2.1%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFSO_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-22">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most of the population (as of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) speaks German (104,465 or 81.2%) as their first language, Italian is the second most common (5,062 or 3.9%) and French is the third (4,671 or 3.6%). There are 171 people who speak <a href="/wiki/Romansh_language" title="Romansh language">Romansh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STAT2000_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-STAT2000-23">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the population was 47.5% male and 52.5% female. The population was made up of 44,032 Swiss men (35.4% of the population) and 15,092 (12.1%) non-Swiss men. There were 51,531 Swiss women (41.4%) and 13,726 (11.0%) non-Swiss women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BE_Stat_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-BE_Stat-24">[21]</a></sup> Of the population in the municipality, 39,008 or about 30.3% were born in Bern and lived there in 2000. There were 27,573 or 21.4% who were born in the same canton, while 25,818 or 20.1% were born somewhere else in Switzerland, and 27,812 or 21.6% were born outside of Switzerland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STAT2000_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-STAT2000-23">[20]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bern_Bethlehem2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="596" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bern_Bethlehem2.jpg/220px-Bern_Bethlehem2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bern_Bethlehem2.jpg/330px-Bern_Bethlehem2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Bern_Bethlehem2.jpg/440px-Bern_Bethlehem2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bern_Bethlehem2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Apartment blocks at Bern-Bethlehem</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, children and teenagers (0–19 years old) make up 15.1% of the population, while adults (20–64 years old) make up 65% and seniors (over 64 years old) make up 19.9%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFSO_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-22">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 59,948 people who were single and never married in the municipality. There were 49,873 married individuals, 9,345 widows or widowers and 9,468 individuals who are divorced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STAT2000_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-STAT2000-23">[20]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Houses_in_the_Old_City_of_Bern.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="901" data-file-width="1600" height="96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Houses_in_the_Old_City_of_Bern.jpg/170px-Houses_in_the_Old_City_of_Bern.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Houses_in_the_Old_City_of_Bern.jpg/255px-Houses_in_the_Old_City_of_Bern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Houses_in_the_Old_City_of_Bern.jpg/340px-Houses_in_the_Old_City_of_Bern.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Houses_in_the_Old_City_of_Bern.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Houses in the Old City of Bern</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 67,115 private households in the municipality, and an average of 1.8 persons per household.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFSO_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-22">[19]</a></sup> There were 34,981 households that consist of only one person and 1,592 households with five or more people. In 2000<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, a total of 65,538 apartments (90.6% of the total) were permanently occupied, while 5,352 apartments (7.4%) were seasonally occupied and 1,444 apartments (2.0%) were empty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Housing_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Housing-25">[22]</a></sup> As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the construction rate of new housing units was 1.2 new units per 1000 residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFSO_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-22">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2003<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the average price to rent an average apartment in Bern was 1108.92 <a href="/wiki/Swiss_franc" title="Swiss franc">Swiss francs</a> (CHF) per month (US$890, £500, €710 approx. exchange rate from 2003). The average rate for a one-room apartment was 619.82 CHF (US$500, £280, €400), a two-room apartment was about 879.36 CHF (US$700, £400, €560), a three-room apartment was about 1040.54 CHF (US$830, £470, €670) and a six or more room apartment cost an average of 2094.80 CHF (US$1680, £940, €1340). The average apartment price in Bern was 99.4% of the national average of 1116 CHF.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BFS_rent_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-BFS_rent-26">[23]</a></sup> The vacancy rate for the municipality, in 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, was 0.45%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFSO_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-22">[19]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From the 2000 census<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 60,455 or 47.0% belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Reformed_Church" title="Swiss Reformed Church">Swiss Reformed Church</a>, while 31,510 or 24.5% were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>. Of the rest of the population, there were 1,874 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" title="Orthodox Christianity">members of an Orthodox church</a> (or about 1.46% of the population), there were 229 persons (or about 0.18% of the population) who belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Catholic_Church_of_Switzerland" title="Christian Catholic Church of Switzerland">Christian Catholic Church</a>, and there were 5,531 persons (or about 4.30% of the population) who belonged to another Christian church. There were 324 persons (or about 0.25% of the population) who were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a>, and 4,907 (or about 3.81% of the population) who were <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>. There were 629 persons who were <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a>, 1,430 persons who were <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu</a> and 177 persons who belonged to another church. 16,363 (or about 12.72% of the population) belonged to no church, are agnostic or <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheist</a>, and 7,855 persons (or about 6.11% of the population) did not answer the question.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STAT2000_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-STAT2000-23">[20]</a></sup> On 14 December 2014 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haus_der_Religionen" title="Haus der Religionen">Haus der Religionen</a> was inaugurated.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Federal_Palace_of_Switzerland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Federal_Palace_of_Switzerland.jpg/220px-Federal_Palace_of_Switzerland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Federal_Palace_of_Switzerland.jpg/330px-Federal_Palace_of_Switzerland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Federal_Palace_of_Switzerland.jpg/440px-Federal_Palace_of_Switzerland.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Federal_Palace_of_Switzerland.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Federal Palace of Switzerland (Swiss Parliament Building)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:4377_-_Bern_-_Kindlifresserbrunnen_am_Kornhausplatz.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2736" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/4377_-_Bern_-_Kindlifresserbrunnen_am_Kornhausplatz.JPG/100px-4377_-_Bern_-_Kindlifresserbrunnen_am_Kornhausplatz.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/4377_-_Bern_-_Kindlifresserbrunnen_am_Kornhausplatz.JPG/150px-4377_-_Bern_-_Kindlifresserbrunnen_am_Kornhausplatz.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/4377_-_Bern_-_Kindlifresserbrunnen_am_Kornhausplatz.JPG/200px-4377_-_Bern_-_Kindlifresserbrunnen_am_Kornhausplatz.JPG 2x" width="100"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:4377_-_Bern_-_Kindlifresserbrunnen_am_Kornhausplatz.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Ogre of the Kindlifresserbrunnen has a sack of children waiting to be devoured.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The structure of Bern's <a href="/wiki/Old_City_of_Bern" title="Old City of Bern">city centre</a> is largely <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval" title="Medieval">medieval</a> and has been recognised by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> as a Cultural <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>. Perhaps its most famous sight is the <i><a href="/wiki/Zytglogge" title="Zytglogge">Zytglogge</a></i> (Bernese German for "Time Bell"), an elaborate medieval clock tower with moving puppets. It also has an impressive 15th century <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> cathedral, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnster_(Bern)" title="Münster (Bern)">Münster</a></i>, and a 15th-century town hall. Thanks to 6 kilometres (4 miles) of arcades, the old town boasts one of the longest covered shopping promenades in Europe.</p>
<p>Since the 16th century, the city has had a bear pit, the <i><a href="/wiki/B%C3%A4rengraben" title="Bärengraben">Bärengraben</a></i>, at the far end of the <a href="/wiki/Nydeggbr%C3%BCcke" title="Nydeggbrücke">Nydeggbrücke</a> to house its heraldic animals. The currently four bears are now kept in an open-air enclosure nearby, and two other young bears, a present by the Russian president, are kept in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D%C3%A4hlh%C3%B6lzli" title="Dählhölzli">Dählhölzli</a> zoo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Federal Palace (<a href="/wiki/Federal_Palace_of_Switzerland" title="Federal Palace of Switzerland">Bundeshaus</a>), built from 1857 to 1902, which houses the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Assembly" title="Swiss Federal Assembly">national parliament</a>, government and part of the federal administration, can also be visited.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a> lived in a flat at the <a href="/wiki/Kramgasse" title="Kramgasse">Kramgasse</a> 49, the site of the <a href="/wiki/Einsteinhaus" title="Einsteinhaus">Einsteinhaus</a>, from 1903 to 1905, the year in which the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annus_Mirabilis_Papers" title="Annus Mirabilis Papers">Annus Mirabilis Papers</a> were published.</p>
<p>The Rose Garden (<i>Rosengarten</i>), from which a scenic panoramic view of the medieval town centre can be enjoyed, is a well-kept Rosarium on a hill, converted into a park from a former cemetery in 1913.</p>
<p>There are <a href="/wiki/List_of_fountains_in_Bern" title="List of fountains in Bern">eleven Renaissance allegorical statues</a> on public fountains in the Old Town. Nearly all the 16th century fountains, except the <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%A4hringerbrunnen" title="Zähringerbrunnen">Zähringer fountain</a> which was created by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hans_Hiltbrand&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hans Hiltbrand (page does not exist)">Hans Hiltbrand</a>, are the work of the <a href="/wiki/Fribourg" title="Fribourg">Fribourg</a> master <a href="/wiki/Hans_Gieng" title="Hans Gieng">Hans Gieng</a>. One of the more interesting fountains is the <a href="/wiki/Kindlifresserbrunnen" title="Kindlifresserbrunnen">Kindlifresserbrunnen</a> (Bernese German: Child Eater Fountain but often translated <a href="/wiki/Ogre" title="Ogre">Ogre</a> Fountain) which is claimed to represent a Jew,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[26]</a></sup> the Greek god <a href="/wiki/Chronos" title="Chronos">Chronos</a> or a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swabian-Alemannic-Fastnacht" title="Swabian-Alemannic-Fastnacht">Fastnacht</a> figure that scares disobedient children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bern's most recent sight is the set of fountains in front of the Federal Palace. It was inaugurated on 1 August 2004.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Universal_Postal_Union" title="Universal Postal Union">Universal Postal Union</a> is situated in Bern.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Zytglogge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="899" data-file-width="1600" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_Zytglogge.jpg/220px-The_Zytglogge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_Zytglogge.jpg/330px-The_Zytglogge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_Zytglogge.jpg/440px-The_Zytglogge.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Zytglogge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Zytglogge" title="Zytglogge">Zytglogge</a> clock tower and the city's medieval covered shopping promenades (<i>Lauben</i>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heritage_sites_of_national_significance">Heritage sites of national significance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Heritage sites of national significance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bern is home to 114 Swiss <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_inventory_of_cultural_property_of_national_and_regional_significance" title="Swiss inventory of cultural property of national and regional significance">heritage sites of national significance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>It includes the entire <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Town_of_Bern" title="Old Town of Bern">Old Town</a>, which is also a UNESCO World Heritage Site, and many sites within and around it. Some of the most notable in the Old Town include the <a href="/wiki/Bern_Minster" title="Bern Minster">Cathedral</a> which was started in 1421 and is the tallest cathedral in Switzerland, the <a href="/wiki/Zytglogge" title="Zytglogge">Zytglogge</a> and <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A4figturm" title="Käfigturm">Käfigturm</a> towers, which mark two successive expansions of the Old Town, and the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Ghost,_Bern" title="Church of the Holy Ghost, Bern">Holy Ghost Church</a>, which is one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Reformed_Church" title="Swiss Reformed Church">Swiss Reformed</a> churches in Switzerland. Within the Old Town, there are eleven <a href="/wiki/List_of_fountains_in_Bern" title="List of fountains in Bern">16th century fountains</a>, most attributed to <a href="/wiki/Hans_Gieng" title="Hans Gieng">Hans Gieng</a>, that are on the list.</p>
<p>Outside the Old Town the heritage sites include the Bärengraben, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gewerbeschule_Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gewerbeschule Bern (page does not exist)">Gewerbeschule Bern</a> (1937), the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Eidgen%C3%B6ssisches_Archiv_f%C3%BCr_Denkmalpflege&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Eidgenössisches Archiv für Denkmalpflege (page does not exist)">Eidgenössisches Archiv für Denkmalpflege</a>, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kirchenfeld&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kirchenfeld (page does not exist)">Kirchenfeld</a> mansion district (after 1881), the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Thunplatzbrunnen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Thunplatzbrunnen (page does not exist)">Thunplatzbrunnen</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Swissmint" title="Swissmint">Federal Mint</a> building, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Archives" title="Swiss Federal Archives">Federal Archives</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_National_Library" title="Swiss National Library">Swiss National Library</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historical_Museum_of_Bern" title="Historical Museum of Bern">Historical Museum</a> (1894), <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alpine_Museum_of_Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alpine Museum of Bern (page does not exist)">Alpine Museum</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Museum_of_Communication,_Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Museum of Communication, Bern (page does not exist)">Museum of Communication</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_History_Museum_of_Bern" title="Natural History Museum of Bern">Natural History Museum</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinemas">Cinemas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Cinemas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bern has several dozen cinemas. As is customary in Switzerland, films are generally shown in their original language (e.g., English) with German and French subtitles. Only a small number of screenings are dubbed in German.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_festivals">Film festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Film festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shnit_international_shortfilmfestival" title="Shnit international shortfilmfestival">Shnit international shortfilmfestival</a> shnit International Shortfilmfestival, held annually in early October.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Queersicht" title="Queersicht">Queersicht</a> – gay and lesbian film festival, held annually in the second week of November.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
<p>Bern was the site of the <a href="/wiki/1954_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="1954 FIFA World Cup Final">1954 Football (Soccer) World Cup Final</a>, a huge upset for the Hungarian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magical_Magyars" title="Magical Magyars">Golden Team</a>, who were beaten 3–2 by West Germany. The football team <a href="/wiki/BSC_Young_Boys" title="BSC Young Boys">BSC Young Boys</a> is based in Bern at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stade_de_Suisse,_Wankdorf" title="Stade de Suisse, Wankdorf">Stade de Suisse Wankdorf</a>, which also was one of the venues for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008" title="UEFA Euro 2008">European football championship 2008</a> in which it hosted 3 matches.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/SC_Bern" title="SC Bern">SC Bern</a> is the major ice hockey team of Bern who plays at the <a href="/wiki/PostFinance_Arena" title="PostFinance Arena">PostFinance Arena</a>. The team has ranked highest in attendance for a European hockey team for more than a decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCBernAttendence_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-SCBernAttendence-37">[34]</a></sup> The PostFinance Arena was the main host of the <a href="/wiki/2009_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2009 IIHF World Championship">2009 IIHF Ice Hockey World Championship</a>, including the opening game and the final of the tournament.</p>
<p>The PostFinance Arena was also the host of the 2011 European Figure Skate Championships.</p>
<p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bern_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bern Cardinals (page does not exist)">Bern Cardinals</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">baseball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">softball</a> team of Bern, which plays at the Allmend</p>
<p>Bern Grizzlies is the American football club in Bern and plays at Athletics Arena Wankdorf.</p>
<p>Bern was a candidate to host the 2010 Winter Olympics, but withdrew its bid in September 2002 after a referendum was passed that showed that the bid was not supported by locals. Those games were eventually awarded to <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver, British Columbia</a>, Canada.</p>
<p>RC Bern is the local rugby club (since 1972) and plays at the Allmend. The ladies team was founded in 1995.</p>
<p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bern_Bears&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bern Bears (page does not exist)">Bern Bears</a> is an NGO Basketball Club since 2010 in city of Bern.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stadt_Bern_1897.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="9175" data-file-width="6041" height="334" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Stadt_Bern_1897.jpg/220px-Stadt_Bern_1897.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Stadt_Bern_1897.jpg/330px-Stadt_Bern_1897.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Stadt_Bern_1897.jpg/440px-Stadt_Bern_1897.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stadt_Bern_1897.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bond of the Einwohnergemeinde der Stadt Bern, issued 1. April 1897</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Bern had an unemployment rate of 3.3%. As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 259 people employed in the <a href="/wiki/Primary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Primary sector of the economy">primary economic sector</a> and about 59 businesses involved in this sector. 16,413 people were employed in the <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Secondary sector of the economy">secondary sector</a> and there were 950 businesses in this sector. 135,973 people were employed in the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">tertiary sector</a>, with 7,654 businesses in this sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFSO_22-5"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-22">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the total number of <a href="/wiki/Full-time_equivalent" title="Full-time equivalent">full-time equivalent</a> jobs was 125,037. The number of jobs in the primary sector was 203, of which 184 were in agriculture and 19 were in forestry or lumber production. The number of jobs in the secondary sector was 15,476 of which 7,650 or (49.4%) were in manufacturing, 51 or (0.3%) were in mining and 6,389 (41.3%) were in construction. The number of jobs in the tertiary sector was 109,358. In the tertiary sector; 11,396 or 10.4% were in wholesale or retail sales or the repair of motor vehicles, 10,293 or 9.4% were in the movement and storage of goods, 5,090 or 4.7% were in a hotel or restaurant, 7,302 or 6.7% were in the information industry, 8,437 or 7.7% were the insurance or financial industry, 10,660 or 9.7% were technical professionals or scientists, 5,338 or 4.9% were in education and 17,903 or 16.4% were in health care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 94,367 workers who commuted into the municipality and 16,424 workers who commuted away. The municipality is a net importer of workers, with about 5.7 workers entering the municipality for every one leaving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commuter_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-commuter-40">[37]</a></sup> Of the working population, 50.6% used public transport to get to work, and 20.6% used a private car.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SFSO_22-6"><a href="#cite_note-SFSO-22">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Universit%C3%A4t_Bern_Hauptgeb%C3%A4ude_DSC05758.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2068" data-file-width="3740" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Universit%C3%A4t_Bern_Hauptgeb%C3%A4ude_DSC05758.jpg/220px-Universit%C3%A4t_Bern_Hauptgeb%C3%A4ude_DSC05758.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Universit%C3%A4t_Bern_Hauptgeb%C3%A4ude_DSC05758.jpg/330px-Universit%C3%A4t_Bern_Hauptgeb%C3%A4ude_DSC05758.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Universit%C3%A4t_Bern_Hauptgeb%C3%A4ude_DSC05758.jpg/440px-Universit%C3%A4t_Bern_Hauptgeb%C3%A4ude_DSC05758.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Universit%C3%A4t_Bern_Hauptgeb%C3%A4ude_DSC05758.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Main building of the University of Bern</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bern" title="University of Bern">University of Bern</a>, whose buildings are mainly located in the <i>Länggasse</i> quarter, is located in Bern, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Bern_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Bern University of Applied Sciences">University of Applied Sciences</a> (<i>Fachhochschule</i>) and several vocations schools.</p>
<p>In Bern, about 50,418 or (39.2%) of the population have completed non-mandatory <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Switzerland#Secondary" title="Education in Switzerland">upper secondary education</a>, and 24,311 or (18.9%) have completed additional higher education (either <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Switzerland" title="List of universities in Switzerland">university</a> or a <i><a href="/wiki/Fachhochschule" title="Fachhochschule">Fachhochschule</a></i>). Of the 24,311 who completed tertiary schooling, 51.6% were Swiss men, 33.0% were Swiss women, 8.9% were non-Swiss men and 6.5% were non-Swiss women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STAT2000_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-STAT2000-23">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The canton of Bern school system provides one year of non-obligatory <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a>, followed by six years of primary school. This is followed by three years of obligatory lower secondary school where the pupils are separated according to ability and aptitude. Following the lower secondary pupils may attend additional schooling or they may enter an <a href="/wiki/Apprenticeship" title="Apprenticeship">apprenticeship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 2009–10 school year, there were a total of 10,979 pupils attending classes in Bern. There were 89 kindergarten classes with a total of 1,641 pupils in the municipality. Of the kindergarten pupils, 32.4% were permanent or temporary residents of Switzerland (not citizens) and 40.2% have a different mother language than the classroom language. The municipality had 266 primary classes and 5,040 pupils. Of the primary pupils, 30.1% were permanent or temporary residents of Switzerland (not citizens) and 35.7% have a different mother language than the classroom language. During the same year, there were 151 lower secondary classes with a total of 2,581 pupils. There were 28.7% who were permanent or temporary residents of Switzerland (not citizens) and 32.7% have a different mother language than the classroom language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-School_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-School-42">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bern is home to 8 libraries. These libraries include; the Schweiz. Nationalbibliothek/ Bibliothèque nationale suisse, the <i>Universitätsbibliothek Bern</i>, the <i>Kornhausbibliotheken Bern</i>, the <i>BFH Wirtschaft und Verwaltung Bern</i>, the <i>BFH Gesundheit</i>, the <i>BFH Soziale Arbeit</i>, the <i>Hochschule der Künste Bern, Gestaltung und Kunst</i> and the <i>Hochschule der Künste Bern, Musikbibliothek</i>. There was a combined total (as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>) of 10,308,336 books or other media in the libraries, and in the same year a total of 2,627,973 items were loaned out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2000<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 9,045 pupils in Bern who came from another municipality, while 1,185 residents attended schools outside the municipality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commuter_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-commuter-40">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Combino_Bern.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Combino_Bern.jpg/220px-Combino_Bern.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Combino_Bern.jpg/330px-Combino_Bern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Combino_Bern.jpg/440px-Combino_Bern.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Combino_Bern.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Bern" title="Trams in Bern">Tram station</a> on the Bahnhofplatz, with the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Ghost,_Bern" title="Church of the Holy Ghost, Bern">Heiliggeistkirche</a> in the background</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The public transport in and around Bern is operated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bernmobil" title="Bernmobil">BERNMOBIL</a>, which is integrated into the fare network <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Libero_(fare_network)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Libero (fare network) (page does not exist)">libero</a> with coordinated timetables, which in itself covers the area of canton of Bern and <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Solothurn" title="Canton of Solothurn">Solothurn</a>. The fare network includes any mode of public transport, such as any kind of train (including the urban <a href="/wiki/Bern_S-Bahn" title="Bern S-Bahn">S-Bahn</a>), <a href="/wiki/PostBus_Switzerland" title="PostBus Switzerland">PostAuto buses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Bern" title="Trams in Bern">trams</a>, buses (either <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Bern" title="Trolleybuses in Bern">trolleybuses</a> or motorized buses) and others. Fares are based on the number of zones crossed during a specified time and are independent of the mode of transport or the number of connections. The central part of Bern, excluding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B%C3%BCmpliz" title="Bümpliz">Bümpliz</a>, <i>Betlehem</i>, <i>Bottingen</i>, <i>Brünnen</i>, and <i>Riedbach</i> in the west of the municipality, is part of the fare zone <i>100</i>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bern_railway_station" title="Bern railway station">Bern's central railway station <i>Bahnhof Bern</i>)</a> (formerly known as <i>Hauptbahnhof Bern</i>) is not only the central network nucleus of Bern, but also of the whole urban and inter-cantonal region. It connects the city to the urban, national and international railways network and is Switzerland's second most busy railway station (202,600 passengers per working day in 2014).</p>
<p>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Funicular_railway" title="Funicular railway">funicular railway</a> leads from the <i>Marzili</i> district to the <i>Bundeshaus</i>. The <a href="/wiki/Marzilibahn_funicular" title="Marzilibahn funicular">Marzilibahn funicular</a> is, with a length of 106 m (348 ft), the second shortest public railway in Europe after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zagreb_funicular" title="Zagreb funicular">Zagreb funicular</a>.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Aar_bridges_in_Bern" title="List of Aar bridges in Bern">Several Aare bridges</a> connect the old parts of the city with the newer districts outside of the peninsula.</p>
<p>Bern is well connected to other cities by several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autobahns_of_Switzerland" title="Autobahns of Switzerland">motorways</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A1_(Switzerland)" title="A1 (Switzerland)">A1</a>, A12, A6).</p>
<p>Bern is also served by <a href="/wiki/Bern_Airport" title="Bern Airport">Bern Airport</a>, located outside the city near the town of <a href="/wiki/Belp" title="Belp">Belp</a>. The regional airport, colloquially called <i>Bern-Belp</i> or <i>Belpmoos</i>, is connected to several European cities. Additionally <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich_Airport" title="Zürich Airport">Zürich Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Airport" title="Geneva Airport">Geneva Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/EuroAirport_Basel_Mulhouse_Freiburg" title="EuroAirport Basel Mulhouse Freiburg">EuroAirport Basel Mulhouse Freiburg</a> also serve as international gateways, all reachable within less than two hours by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SBB_CFF_FFS" title="SBB CFF FFS">train</a> or car from Bern.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Einsteinhausberne.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2b/Einsteinhausberne.jpg/220px-Einsteinhausberne.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2b/Einsteinhausberne.jpg/330px-Einsteinhausberne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2b/Einsteinhausberne.jpg/440px-Einsteinhausberne.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Einsteinhausberne.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Albert Einstein's house</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Bakunin" title="Mikhail Bakunin">Mikhail Bakunin</a>, died in Bern on 1 July 1876</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peter_Bieri_(author)" title="Peter Bieri (author)">Peter Bieri</a>, philosophy professor and novelist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Louise_Elisabeth_de_Meuron" title="Louise Elisabeth de Meuron">Louise Elisabeth de Meuron</a>, famed eccentric and noble lady</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a>, worked out his <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_relativity" title="Theory of relativity">theory of relativity</a> while living in Bern, employed as a <a href="/wiki/Patent_examiner" title="Patent examiner">patent examiner</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Institute_of_Intellectual_Property" title="Swiss Federal Institute of Intellectual Property">patent office</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Emmert" title="Paul Emmert">Paul Emmert</a>, painter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christoph_von_Graffenried" title="Christoph von Graffenried">Christoph von Graffenried</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/New_Bern,_North_Carolina" title="New Bern, North Carolina">New Bern</a> in the U.S. state of <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Albrecht_von_Haller" title="Albrecht von Haller">Albrecht von Haller</a></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Emil_Theodor_Kocher" title="Emil Theodor Kocher">Emil Theodor Kocher</a>, recipient of 1909 Nobel Prize</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a>, resided in Bern from 1914 until 1917</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mani_Matter" title="Mani Matter">Mani Matter</a>, songwriter</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Algirdas_Paleckis" title="Algirdas Paleckis">Algirdas Paleckis</a>, diplomat and politician, born in Bern</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Regula_Rytz" title="Regula Rytz">Regula Rytz</a> (born 1962),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-woz-20111110_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-woz-20111110-44">[41]</a></sup> politician, sociologist and historian</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9on_Savary" title="Léon Savary">Léon Savary</a>, Swiss writer and journalist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mark_Streit" title="Mark Streit">Mark Streit</a>, ice hockey player</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aim%C3%A9_F%C3%A9lix_Tschiffely" title="Aimé Félix Tschiffely">Aimé Félix Tschiffely</a>, famous equestrian</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hans_Urwyler" title="Hans Urwyler">Hans Urwyler</a>, Christian minister</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adolf_W%C3%B6lfli" title="Adolf Wölfli">Adolf Wölfli</a>, visual artist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ursula_Wyss" title="Ursula Wyss">Ursula Wyss</a>, economist and politician</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes_and_references">Notes and references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Notes and references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the Swiss constitution, there is intentionally no <i>capital</i> in the Swiss Confederation, but Bern has governmental institutions such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_parliament" title="Swiss parliament">Swiss parliament</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Council_of_Switzerland" title="Federal Council of Switzerland">Federal Council of Switzerland</a>. However, The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Supreme_Court_of_Switzerland" title="Federal Supreme Court of Switzerland">Federal Supreme Court of Switzerland</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Lausanne" title="Lausanne">Lausanne</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Criminal_Court_of_Switzerland" title="Federal Criminal Court of Switzerland">Federal Criminal Court of Switzerland</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Bellinzona" title="Bellinzona">Bellinzona</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Administrative_Court_of_Switzerland" title="Federal Administrative Court of Switzerland">Federal Administrative Court of Switzerland</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Patent_Court_of_Switzerland" title="Federal Patent Court of Switzerland">Federal Patent Court of Switzerland</a> are in <a href="/wiki/St._Gallen" title="St. Gallen">St. Gallen</a>. That exemplifies the very federal nature of the Swiss Confederation</span></li>
</ol>
</div>

"Die Hauptstadt existiert nicht" [The capital does not exist]. UniPress (in German) (UniPress 152: Die Hauptstatdtregion). Berne: University of Berne: 16–19. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.7892%2Fboris.41280" rel="nofollow">10.7892/boris.41280</a>. <q>Als 1848 ein politisch-administratives Zentrum für den neuen Bundesstaat zu bestimmen war, verzichteten die Verfassungsväter darauf, eine Hauptstadt der Schweiz zu bezeichnen und formulierten stattdessen in Artikel 108: «Alles, was sich auf den Sitz der Bundesbehörden bezieht, ist Gegenstand der Bundesgesetzgebung.» Die Bundesstadt ist also nicht mehr und nicht weniger als der Sitz der Bundesbehörden.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABern&amp;rft.atitle=Die+Hauptstadt+existiert+nicht&amp;rft.aufirst=Andr%C3%A9&amp;rft.aulast=Holenstein&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.7892%2Fboris.41280&amp;rft.issue=UniPress+152%3A+Die+Hauptstatdtregion&amp;rft.pages=16-19&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
